err != nil {\n\t\tisAccessor = false\n\t}\n\tisList := meta.IsListType(obj)\n\t_, isTable := obj.(*metav1.Table)\n\tif !isAccessor && !isList && !isTable {\n\t\treturn nil, false, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// TODO a deep copy isn't really needed here, figure out how we can reliably\n\t//  use shallow copy here to omit the manageFields.\n\tcopy := obj.DeepCopyObject()\n\n\tif isAccessor {\n\t\tif err := removeManagedFields(copy); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, false, err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif isList {\n\t\tif err := meta.EachListItem(copy, removeManagedFields); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, false, err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif isTable {\n\t\ttable := copy.(*metav1.Table)\n\t\tfor i := range table.Rows {\n\t\t\trowObj := table.Rows[i].Object\n\t\t\tif err := removeManagedFields(rowObj.Object); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn nil, false, err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn copy, true, nil\n}\n\nfunc removeManagedFields(obj runtime.Object) error {\n\tif obj == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\taccessor, err := meta.Accessor(obj)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\taccessor.SetManagedFields(nil)\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc shouldOmitManagedFields(ctx context.Context) bool {\n\tif auditContext := AuditContextFrom(ctx); auditContext != nil {\n\t\treturn auditContext.RequestAuditConfig.OmitManagedFields\n\t}\n\n\t// If we can't decide, return false to maintain current behavior which is\n\t// to retain the manage fields in the audit.\n\treturn false\n}\n","numLines":313,"startLine":1,"totalLines":313}}}

longRunningSink, ev, omitStages)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tev.Stage = auditinternal.StageResponseComplete\n\t\t\tif ev.ResponseStatus == nil {\n\t\t\t\tev.ResponseStatus = fakedSuccessStatus\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tprocessAuditEvent(ctx, sink, ev, omitStages)\n\t\t}()\n\t\thandler.ServeHTTP(respWriter, req)\n\t})\n}\n\n// evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent is responsible for evaluating the audit\n// policy configuration applicable to the request and create a new audit\n// event that will be written to the API audit log.\n// - error if anything bad happened\nfunc evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent(req *http.Request, policy audit.PolicyRuleEvaluator) (*audit.AuditContext, error) {\n\tctx := req.Context()\n\tac := audit.AuditContextFrom(ctx)\n\tif ac == nil {\n\t\t// Auditing not configured.\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\n\tattribs, err := GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn ac, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to GetAuthorizerAttributes: %v\", err)\n\t}\n\n\trac := policy.EvaluatePolicyRule(attribs)\n\taudit.ObservePolicyLevel(ctx, rac.Level)\n\tac.RequestAuditConfig = rac\n\tif rac.Level == auditinternal.LevelNone {\n\t\t// Don't audit.\n\t\treturn ac, nil\n\t}\n\n\trequestReceivedTimestamp, ok := request.ReceivedTimestampFrom(ctx)\n\tif !ok {\n\t\trequestReceivedTimestamp = time.Now()\n\t}\n\taudit.LogRequestMetadata(ctx, req, requestReceivedTimestamp, rac.Level, attribs)\n\n\treturn ac, nil\n}\n\n// writeLatencyToAnnotation writes the latency incurred in different\n// layers of the apiserver to the annotations of the audit object.\n// it should be invoked after ev.StageTimestamp has been set appropriately.\nfunc writeLatencyToAnnotation(ctx context.Context, ev *auditinternal.Event) {\n\t// we will track latency in annotation only when the total latency\n\t// of the given request exceeds 500ms, this is in keeping with the\n\t// traces in rest/handlers for create, delete, update,\n\t// get, list, and deletecollection.\n\tconst threshold = 500 * time.Millisecond\n\tlatency := ev.StageTimestamp.Time.Sub(ev.RequestReceivedTimestamp.Time)\n\tif latency <= threshold {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// if we are tracking latency incurred inside different layers within\n\t// the apiserver, add these as annotation to the audit event object.\n\tlayerLatencies := request.AuditAnnotationsFromLatencyTrackers(ctx)\n\tif len(layerLatencies) == 0 {\n\t\t// latency tracking is not enabled for this request\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// record the total latency for this request, for convenience.\n\tlayerLatencies[\"apiserver.latency.k8s.io/total\"] = latency.String()\n\taudit.AddAuditAnnotationsMap(ctx, layerLatencies)\n}\n\nfunc processAuditEvent(ctx context.Context, sink audit.Sink, ev *auditinternal.Event, omitStages []auditinternal.Stage) bool {\n\tfor _, stage := range omitStages {\n\t\tif ev.Stage == stage {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tswitch {\n\tcase ev.Stage == auditinternal.StageRequestReceived:\n\t\tev.StageTimestamp = metav1.NewMicroTime(ev.RequestReceivedTimestamp.Time)\n\tcase ev.Stage == auditinternal.StageResponseComplete:\n\t\tev.StageTimestamp = metav1.NewMicroTime(time.Now())\n\t\twriteLatencyToAnnotation(ctx, ev)\n\tdefault:\n\t\tev.StageTimestamp = metav1.NewMicroTime(time.Now())\n\t}\n\n\taudit.ObserveEvent(ctx)\n\treturn sink.ProcessEvents(ev)\n}\n\nfunc decorateResponseWriter(ctx context.Context, responseWriter http.ResponseWriter, ev *auditinternal.Event, sink audit.Sink, omitStages []auditinternal.Stage) http.ResponseWriter {\n\tdelegate := &auditResponseWriter{\n\t\tctx:            ctx,\n\t\tResponseWriter: responseWriter,\n\t\tevent:          ev,\n\t\tsink:           sink,\n\t\tomitStages:     omitStages,\n\t}\n\n\treturn responsewriter.WrapForHTTP1Or2(delegate)\n}\n\nvar _ http.ResponseWriter = &auditResponseWriter{}\nvar _ responsewriter.UserProvidedDecorator = &auditResponseWriter{}\n\n// auditResponseWriter intercepts WriteHeader, sets it in the event. If the sink is set, it will\n// create immediately an event (for long running requests).\ntype auditResponseWriter struct {\n\thttp.ResponseWriter\n\tctx        context.Context\n\tevent      *auditinternal.Event\n\tonce       sync.Once\n\tsink       audit.Sink\n\tomitStages []auditinternal.Stage\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) Unwrap() http.ResponseWriter {\n\treturn a.ResponseWriter\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) processCode(code int) {\n\ta.once.Do(func() {\n\t\tif a.event.ResponseStatus == nil {\n\t\t\ta.event.ResponseStatus = &metav1.Status{}\n\t\t}\n\t\ta.event.ResponseStatus.Code = int32(code)\n\t\ta.event.Stage = auditinternal.StageResponseStarted\n\n\t\tif a.sink != nil {\n\t\t\tprocessAuditEvent(a.ctx, a.sink, a.event, a.omitStages)\n\t\t}\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) Write(bs []byte) (int, error) {\n\t// the Go library calls WriteHeader internally if no code was written yet. But this will go unnoticed for us\n\ta.processCode(http.StatusOK)\n\treturn a.ResponseWriter.Write(bs)\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) WriteHeader(code int) {\n\ta.processCode(code)\n\ta.ResponseWriter.WriteHeader(code)\n}\n\nfunc (a *auditResponseWriter) Hijack() (net.Conn, *bufio.ReadWriter, error) {\n\t// fake a response status before protocol switch happens\n\ta.processCode(http.StatusSwitchingProtocols)\n\n\t// the outer ResponseWriter object returned by WrapForHTTP1Or2 implements\n\t// http.Hijacker if the inner object (a.ResponseWriter) implements http.Hijacker.\n\treturn a.ResponseWriter.(http.Hijacker).Hijack()\n}\n","numLines":264,"startLine":1,"totalLines":264}}}

{\n\tif policyRule.OmitManagedFields == nil {\n\t\treturn policyDefault\n\t}\n\n\treturn *policyRule.OmitManagedFields\n}\n\n// Check whether the rule matches the request attrs.\nfunc ruleMatches(r *audit.PolicyRule, attrs authorizer.Attributes) bool {\n\tuser := attrs.GetUser()\n\tif len(r.Users) > 0 {\n\t\tif user == nil || !hasString(r.Users, user.GetName()) {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(r.UserGroups) > 0 {\n\t\tif user == nil {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\tmatched := false\n\t\tfor _, group := range user.GetGroups() {\n\t\t\tif hasString(r.UserGroups, group) {\n\t\t\t\tmatched = true\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif !matched {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(r.Verbs) > 0 {\n\t\tif !hasString(r.Verbs, attrs.GetVerb()) {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif len(r.Namespaces) > 0 || len(r.Resources) > 0 {\n\t\treturn ruleMatchesResource(r, attrs)\n\t}\n\n\tif len(r.NonResourceURLs) > 0 {\n\t\treturn ruleMatchesNonResource(r, attrs)\n\t}\n\n\treturn true\n}\n\n// Check whether the rule's non-resource URLs match the request attrs.\nfunc ruleMatchesNonResource(r *audit.PolicyRule, attrs authorizer.Attributes) bool {\n\tif attrs.IsResourceRequest() {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\tpath := attrs.GetPath()\n\tfor _, spec := range r.NonResourceURLs {\n\t\tif pathMatches(path, spec) {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// Check whether the path matches the path specification.\nfunc pathMatches(path, spec string) bool {\n\t// Allow wildcard match\n\tif spec == \"*\" {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\t// Allow exact match\n\tif spec == path {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\t// Allow a trailing * subpath match\n\tif strings.HasSuffix(spec, \"*\") && strings.HasPrefix(path, strings.TrimRight(spec, \"*\")) {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// Check whether the rule's resource fields match the request attrs.\nfunc ruleMatchesResource(r *audit.PolicyRule, attrs authorizer.Attributes) bool {\n\tif !attrs.IsResourceRequest() {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\tif len(r.Namespaces) > 0 {\n\t\tif !hasString(r.Namespaces, attrs.GetNamespace()) { // Non-namespaced resources use the empty string.\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(r.Resources) == 0 {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\n\tapiGroup := attrs.GetAPIGroup()\n\tresource := attrs.GetResource()\n\tsubresource := attrs.GetSubresource()\n\tcombinedResource := resource\n\t// If subresource, the resource in the policy must match \"(resource)/(subresource)\"\n\tif subresource != \"\" {\n\t\tcombinedResource = resource + \"/\" + subresource\n\t}\n\n\tname := attrs.GetName()\n\n\tfor _, gr := range r.Resources {\n\t\tif gr.Group == apiGroup {\n\t\t\tif len(gr.Resources) == 0 {\n\t\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor _, res := range gr.Resources {\n\t\t\t\tif len(gr.ResourceNames) == 0 || hasString(gr.ResourceNames, name) {\n\t\t\t\t\t// match \"*\"\n\t\t\t\t\tif res == combinedResource || res == \"*\" {\n\t\t\t\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\t// match \"*/subresource\"\n\t\t\t\t\tif len(subresource) > 0 && strings.HasPrefix(res, \"*/\") && subresource == strings.TrimPrefix(res, \"*/\") {\n\t\t\t\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\t// match \"resource/*\"\n\t\t\t\t\tif strings.HasSuffix(res, \"/*\") && resource == strings.TrimSuffix(res, \"/*\") {\n\t\t\t\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// Utility function to check whether a string slice contains a string.\nfunc hasString(slice []string, value string) bool {\n\tfor _, s := range slice {\n\t\tif s == value {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\ntype fakePolicyRuleEvaluator struct {\n\tlevel audit.Level\n\tstage []audit.Stage\n}\n\nfunc (f *fakePolicyRuleEvaluator) EvaluatePolicyRule(_ authorizer.Attributes) auditinternal.RequestAuditConfig {\n\treturn auditinternal.RequestAuditConfig{\n\t\tLevel:      f.level,\n\t\tOmitStages: f.stage,\n\t}\n}\n","numLines":240,"startLine":1,"totalLines":240}}}

53→}\n    54→\n    55→type bufferedBackend struct {\n    56→\t// The delegate backend that actually exports events.\n    57→\tdelegateBackend audit.Backend\n    58→\n    59→\t// Channel to buffer 63→\t// Amount of time to wait after sending a batch to the delegate backend before sending another one.\n    64→\t//\n    65→\t// Receiving maxBatchSize events will always trigger sending a batch, 109→\t\tdefer close(b.shutdownCh)\n   110→\n   111→\t\tb.processIncomingEvents(stopCh)\n   112→\n   113→\t\t// Handle the events that were received after the last buffer\n   114→\t\t// scraping and When\n   153→// b.stopCh is closed, processIncomingEvents stops and closes the buffer.\n   154→func (b *bufferedBackend) processIncomingEvents(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n   155→\tdefer close(b.buffer)\n   156→\n   157→\tvar (\n   158→\t\tmaxWaitChan  <-chan time.Time\n   159→\t\tmaxWaitTimer *time.Timer\n   160→\t)\n   161→\t// Only use max wait batching if batching is enabled.\n   162→\tif b.maxBatchSize > 1 {\n   163→\t\tmaxWaitTimer = time.NewTimer(b.maxBatchWait)\n   164→\t\tmaxWaitChan = maxWaitTimer.C\n   165→\t\tdefer maxWaitTimer.Stop()\n   166→\t}\n   167→\n   168→\tfor {\n   169→\t\tfunc() {\n   170→\t\t\t// Recover from any panics caused by this function so a panic in the\n   171→\t\t\t// goroutine can't bring down the main routine.\n   172→\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n   173→\n   174→\t\t\tif b.maxBatchSize > 1 {\n   175→\t\t\t\tmaxWaitTimer.Reset(b.maxBatchWait)\n   176→\t\t\t}\n   177→\t\t\tb.processEvents(b.collectEvents(maxWaitChan, stopCh))\n   178→\t\t}()\n   179→\n   180→\t\tselect {\n   181→\t\tcase <-stopCh:\n   182→\t\t\treturn\n   183→\t\tdefault:\n   184→\t\t}\n   185→\t}\n   186→}\n   187→\n   188→// collectEvents attempts to collect some number of events in a batch.\n   189→//\n   190→// The following things can cause collectEvents to stop and return the list\n   191→// of events:\n   192→//\n   193→//   - Maximum number of events for a batch.\n   194→//   - Timer has passed.\n   195→//   - Buffer channel is closed and empty.\n   196→//   - stopCh is closed.\n   197→func (b *bufferedBackend) collectEvents(timer <-chan time.Time, stopCh <-chan struct{}) []*auditinternal.Event {\n   198→\tvar events []*auditinternal.Event\n   199→\n   200→L:\n   201→\tfor i := 0; Send currently accumulated batch.\n   214→\t\t\tbreak L\n   215→\t\t}\n   216→\t}\n   217→\n   218→\treturn events\n   219→}\n   220→\n   221→// processEvents process the batch events in a goroutine using delegateBackend's ProcessEvents.\n   222→func (b *bufferedBackend) processEvents(events []*auditinternal.Event) {\n   223→\tif len(events) == 0 {\n   224→\t\treturn\n   225→\t}\n   226→\n   227→\t// TODO(audit): Should control the number of active goroutines\n   228→\t// if one goroutine takes 5 seconds to finish, the number of goroutines can be 5 * defaultBatchThrottleQPS\n   229→\tif b.throttle != nil {\n   230→\t\tb.throttle.Accept()\n   231→\t}\n   232→\n   233→\tif b.asyncDelegate {\n   234→\t\tb.wg.Add(1)\n   235→\t\tgo func() {\n   236→\t\t\tdefer b.wg.Done()\n   237→\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n   238→\n   239→\t\t\t// Execute the real processing in a goroutine to keep it from blocking.\n   240→\t\t\t// This lets the batching routine continue draining the queue immediately.\n   241→\t\t\tb.delegateBackend.ProcessEvents(events...)\n   242→\t\t}()\n   243→\t} else {\n   244→\t\tfunc() {\n   245→\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n   246→\n   247→\t\t\t// Execute the real processing in a goroutine to keep it from blocking.\n   248→\t\t\t// This lets the batching routine continue draining the queue immediately.\n   249→\t\t\tb.delegateBackend.ProcessEvents(events...)\n   250→\t\t}()\n   251→\t}\n   252→}\n   253→\n   254→func (b *bufferedBackend) ProcessEvents(ev ...*auditinternal.Event) bool {\n   255→\t// The following mechanism is in place to support the situation when audit\n   256→\t// events are still coming after the backend was stopped.\n   257→\tvar sendErr error\n   258→\tvar evIndex int\n   259→\n   260→\t// If the delegateBackend was shutdown and the buffer channel was closed, an\n   261→\t// attempt to add an event to it will result in panic that we should\n   262→\t// recover from.\n   263→\tdefer func() {\n   264→\t\tif err := recover(); \"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/apis/audit\"\n\t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit\"\n\t\"k8s.io/client-go/util/flowcontrol\"\n)\n\n// PluginName is the name reported in error metrics.\nconst PluginName = \"buffered\"\n\n// BatchConfig represents batching delegate audit backend configuration.\ntype BatchConfig struct {\n\t// BufferSize defines a size of the buffering queue.\n\tBufferSize int\n\t// MaxBatchSize defines maximum size of a batch.\n\tMaxBatchSize int\n\t// MaxBatchWait indicates the maximum interval between two batches.\n\tMaxBatchWait time.Duration\n\n\t// ThrottleEnable defines whether throttling will be applied to the batching process.\n\tThrottleEnable bool\n\t// ThrottleQPS defines the allowed rate of batches per second sent to the delegate backend.\n\tThrottleQPS float32\n\t// ThrottleBurst defines the maximum number of requests sent to the delegate backend at the same moment in case\n\t// the capacity defined by ThrottleQPS was not utilized.\n\tThrottleBurst int\n\n\t// Whether the delegate backend should be called asynchronously.\n\tAsyncDelegate bool\n}\n\ntype bufferedBackend struct {\n\t// The delegate backend that actually exports events.\n\tdelegateBackend audit.Backend\n\n\t// Channel to buffer events before sending to the delegate backend.\n\tbuffer chan *auditinternal.Event\n\t// Maximum number of events in a batch sent to the delegate backend.\n\tmaxBatchSize int\n\t// Amount of time to wait after sending a batch to the delegate backend before sending another one.\n\t//\n\t// Receiving maxBatchSize events will always trigger sending a batch, regardless of the amount of time passed.\n\tmaxBatchWait time.Duration\n\n\t// Whether the delegate backend should be called asynchronously.\n\tasyncDelegate bool\n\n\t// Channel to signal that the batching routine has processed all remaining events and exited.\n\t// Once `shutdownCh` is closed no new events will be sent to the delegate backend.\n\tshutdownCh chan struct{}\n\n\t// WaitGroup to control the concurrency of sending batches to the delegate backend.\n\t// Worker routine calls Add before sending a batch and\n\t// then spawns a routine that calls Done after batch was processed by the delegate backend.\n\t// This WaitGroup is used to wait for all sending routines to finish before shutting down audit backend.\n\twg sync.WaitGroup\n\n\t// Limits the number of batches sent to the delegate backend per second.\n\tthrottle flowcontrol.RateLimiter\n}\n\nvar _ audit.Backend = &bufferedBackend{}\n\n// NewBackend returns a buffered audit backend that wraps delegate backend.\n// Buffered backend automatically runs and shuts down the delegate backend.\nfunc NewBackend(delegate audit.Backend, config BatchConfig) audit.Backend {\n\tvar throttle flowcontrol.RateLimiter\n\tif config.ThrottleEnable {\n\t\tthrottle = flowcontrol.NewTokenBucketRateLimiter(config.ThrottleQPS, config.ThrottleBurst)\n\t}\n\treturn &bufferedBackend{\n\t\tdelegateBackend: delegate,\n\t\tbuffer:          make(chan *auditinternal.Event, config.BufferSize),\n\t\tmaxBatchSize:    config.MaxBatchSize,\n\t\tmaxBatchWait:    config.MaxBatchWait,\n\t\tasyncDelegate:   config.AsyncDelegate,\n\t\tshutdownCh:      make(chan struct{}),\n\t\twg:              sync.WaitGroup{},\n\t\tthrottle:        throttle,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n\tgo func() {\n\t\t// Signal that the working routine has exited.\n\t\tdefer close(b.shutdownCh)\n\n\t\tb.processIncomingEvents(stopCh)\n\n\t\t// Handle the events that were received after the last buffer\n\t\t// scraping and before this line. Since the buffer is closed, no new\n\t\t// events will come through.\n\t\tallEventsProcessed := false\n\t\ttimer := make(chan time.Time)\n\t\tfor !allEventsProcessed {\n\t\t\tallEventsProcessed = func() bool {\n\t\t\t\t// Recover from any panic in order to try to process all remaining events.\n\t\t\t\t// Note, that in case of a panic, the return value will be false and\n\t\t\t\t// the loop execution will continue.\n\t\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n\n\t\t\t\tevents := b.collectEvents(timer, wait.NeverStop)\n\t\t\t\tb.processEvents(events)\n\t\t\t\treturn len(events) == 0\n\t\t\t}()\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n\treturn b.delegateBackend.Run(stopCh)\n}\n\n// Shutdown blocks until stopCh passed to the Run method is closed and all\n// events added prior to that moment are batched and sent to the delegate backend.\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) Shutdown() {\n\t// Wait until the routine spawned in Run method exits.\n\t<-b.shutdownCh\n\n\t// Wait until all sending routines exit.\n\t//\n\t// - When b.shutdownCh is closed, we know that the goroutine in Run has terminated.\n\t// - This means that processIncomingEvents has terminated.\n\t// - Which means that b.buffer is closed and cannot accept any new events anymore.\n\t// - Because processEvents is called synchronously from the Run goroutine, the waitgroup has its final value.\n\t// Hence wg.Wait will not miss any more outgoing batches.\n\tb.wg.Wait()\n\n\tb.delegateBackend.Shutdown()\n}\n\n// processIncomingEvents runs a loop that collects events from the buffer. When\n// b.stopCh is closed, processIncomingEvents stops and closes the buffer.\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) processIncomingEvents(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n\tdefer close(b.buffer)\n\n\tvar (\n\t\tmaxWaitChan  <-chan time.Time\n\t\tmaxWaitTimer *time.Timer\n\t)\n\t// Only use max wait batching if batching is enabled.\n\tif b.maxBatchSize > 1 {\n\t\tmaxWaitTimer = time.NewTimer(b.maxBatchWait)\n\t\tmaxWaitChan = maxWaitTimer.C\n\t\tdefer maxWaitTimer.Stop()\n\t}\n\n\tfor {\n\t\tfunc() {\n\t\t\t// Recover from any panics caused by this function so a panic in the\n\t\t\t// goroutine can't bring down the main routine.\n\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n\n\t\t\tif b.maxBatchSize > 1 {\n\t\t\t\tmaxWaitTimer.Reset(b.maxBatchWait)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tb.processEvents(b.collectEvents(maxWaitChan, stopCh))\n\t\t}()\n\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-stopCh:\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// collectEvents attempts to collect some number of events in a batch.\n//\n// The following things can cause collectEvents to stop and return the list\n// of events:\n//\n//   - Maximum number of events for a batch.\n//   - Timer has passed.\n//   - Buffer channel is closed and empty.\n//   - stopCh is closed.\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) collectEvents(timer <-chan time.Time, stopCh <-chan struct{}) []*auditinternal.Event {\n\tvar events []*auditinternal.Event\n\nL:\n\tfor i := 0; i < b.maxBatchSize; i++ {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase ev, ok := <-b.buffer:\n\t\t\t// Buffer channel was closed and no new events will follow.\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tbreak L\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tevents = append(events, ev)\n\t\tcase <-timer:\n\t\t\t// Timer has expired. Send currently accumulated batch.\n\t\t\tbreak L\n\t\tcase <-stopCh:\n\t\t\t// Backend has been stopped. Send currently accumulated batch.\n\t\t\tbreak L\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn events\n}\n\n// processEvents process the batch events in a goroutine using delegateBackend's ProcessEvents.\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) processEvents(events []*auditinternal.Event) {\n\tif len(events) == 0 {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// TODO(audit): Should control the number of active goroutines\n\t// if one goroutine takes 5 seconds to finish, the number of goroutines can be 5 * defaultBatchThrottleQPS\n\tif b.throttle != nil {\n\t\tb.throttle.Accept()\n\t}\n\n\tif b.asyncDelegate {\n\t\tb.wg.Add(1)\n\t\tgo func() {\n\t\t\tdefer b.wg.Done()\n\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n\n\t\t\t// Execute the real processing in a goroutine to keep it from blocking.\n\t\t\t// This lets the batching routine continue draining the queue immediately.\n\t\t\tb.delegateBackend.ProcessEvents(events...)\n\t\t}()\n\t} else {\n\t\tfunc() {\n\t\t\tdefer runtime.HandleCrash()\n\n\t\t\t// Execute the real processing in a goroutine to keep it from blocking.\n\t\t\t// This lets the batching routine continue draining the queue immediately.\n\t\t\tb.delegateBackend.ProcessEvents(events...)\n\t\t}()\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) ProcessEvents(ev ...*auditinternal.Event) bool {\n\t// The following mechanism is in place to support the situation when audit\n\t// events are still coming after the backend was stopped.\n\tvar sendErr error\n\tvar evIndex int\n\n\t// If the delegateBackend was shutdown and the buffer channel was closed, an\n\t// attempt to add an event to it will result in panic that we should\n\t// recover from.\n\tdefer func() {\n\t\tif err := recover(); err != nil {\n\t\t\tsendErr = fmt.Errorf(\"audit backend shut down\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif sendErr != nil {\n\t\t\taudit.HandlePluginError(PluginName, sendErr, ev[evIndex:]...)\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n\n\tfor i, e := range ev {\n\t\tevIndex = i\n\t\t// Per the audit.Backend interface these events are reused after being\n\t\t// sent to the Sink. Deep copy and send the copy to the queue.\n\t\tevent := e.DeepCopy()\n\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase b.buffer <- event:\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tsendErr = fmt.Errorf(\"audit buffer queue blocked\")\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn true\n}\n\nfunc (b *bufferedBackend) String() string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%s<%s>\", PluginName, b.delegateBackend)\n}\n","numLines":291,"startLine":1,"totalLines":291}}}

and creates audit events. It works in conjunction with `WithAuditInit` in `pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go` which initializes the audit context and generates/manages audit IDs. The audit context is stored using `WithAuditContext` in `pkg/audit/context.go` and propagated throughout the request lifecycle. The evaluated policy determines the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and which stages to omit.\\n\\n## Audit Backend Dispatch\\nAudit events are dispatched to backends through a composable architecture. The `Union` function in `pkg/audit/union.go` allows multiple backends to be composed together. The three main backend implementations are:\\n- Log backend (`plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go`): Writes events to files in legacy or JSON format\\n- Webhook backend (`plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go`): Sends events to external HTTP endpoints with exponential backoff retry\\n- Buffered backend (`plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go`): Batches events and optionally throttles sending to delegate backends\\n\\nBackend initialization and options are configured in `pkg/server/options/audit.go` which coordinates the selection and composition of backends.\\n\\n## Audit Truncation for Large Bodies\\nThe truncate backend (`plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go`) wraps a delegate backend and removes request/response objects when events exceed `MaxEventSize`, while keeping metadata intact. It calculates event sizes by serializing them and adds an annotation to indicate truncation occurred. Events in a batch are split if they exceed `MaxBatchSize` before being sent to the delegate backend.\\n\\n## Supporting Infrastructure\\nThe audit system uses a scheme and codec factory defined in `pkg/audit/scheme.go` for serializing audit events in both v1 and internal API versions. Event formatting for text output is handled by `pkg/audit/format.go`. Metrics tracking audit events and errors are defined in `pkg/audit/metrics.go`. Audit event types are defined in `pkg/apis/audit/types.go` and `pkg/apis/audit/v1/types.go`.
